Qisas — Retaliation

8 min
The Weapon Condition for Intentional Murder: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Defines qatl al-amd and dispute on lethal instrument

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on the weapon condition for qatl al-amd and apply the differing views to a scenario to determine whether qisas or diyah applies.

Core Idea
Intentional murder requires a weapon that typically kills; Abu Hanifa demands sharpness, the Sahibayn accept any heavy lethal object.

This passage examines one of the classic intra-Hanafi disputes: what weapon qualifies for intentional murder (qatl al-amd). Understanding this ikhtilaf is crucial for distinguishing between cases where qisas applies versus where only diyah (blood money) is due. The difference turns on whether the instrument is sharp or merely heavy and potentially lethal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conditions for qatl al-amd
The text explicitly states two conditions: intentional striking (deliberate intent) and a weapon that ordinarily causes death and dismembers limbs. Note that the second condition is the disputed one.
The first condition (intent) is agreed upon.
2
Locate the disputed condition
The dispute centers on what qualifies as a 'weapon that ordinarily causes death' – must it be sharp (like a sword) or can it be any heavy object that typically kills? This is where Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn diverge.
3
Examine Abu Hanifa's proof
Abu Hanifa relies on mursal hadiths: 'Everything is error except the sword' and 'No qisas except with iron.' These suggest that only sharp, iron-based instruments establish qatl al-amd.
These hadiths are considered mursal (lacking a companion link) but are accepted in Hanafi usul.
4
Examine the Sahibayn's counter-proof
The Sahibayn cite the incident of the Jewish man who killed a slave girl with a stone (not sharp) and the Prophet took qisas. This shows that a heavy stone, even if not sharp, can establish intentional murder.
This is a stronger hadith (from Anas ibn Malik, marfu).
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The difference matters: under Abu Hanifa, striking with a heavy non-sharp object leads only to diyah; under the Sahibayn, it leads to qisas (unless pardoned). The later Hanafi tradition often favors the Sahibayn's view.

Source Text

Dismemberment of limbs is like a sharp instrument from wood, stone, and fire, and its consequence is sin and qisas, except if [the killer's] heirs forgive. And there is no expiation in it. For the occurrence of intentional murder, there are two conditions: first, he strikes intentionally; second, he strikes with a weapon that generally causes death and limbs are dismembered. Like if he strikes with sharp wood or sharp stone that causes limbs to be dismembered. If the stone or wood is not sharp, then intentional murder is not established. Its proof is this mursal hadith: from al-Nu'man ibn Bashir, he said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Everything is error except the sword, and for every error there is blood money.' (a) From this mursal hadith, it is understood that intentional murder is established only with a sword or a sharp instrument like a sword. (2) In another narration: from al-Hasan, he said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'No qisas except with iron.' (b) From this mursal hadith, it is understood that intentional murder is established with any sharp thing, whether it is a sword, wood, or stone. Benefit: According to the Sahibayn, if he strikes with any other heavy thing that is not sharp but generally causes death, then intentional murder is established. For example, if it is a heavy stone or heavy wood that is not sharp, intentional murder is still established. A Jewish man crushed the head of a slave girl with a stone, and the Prophet took qisas from him, which shows that if he strikes with a heavy stone even if not sharp, intentional murder is established and qisas is taken. The hadith portion is: from Anas ibn Malik, he said: A girl wearing ornaments came out in Madinah, and a Jewish man threw a stone at her... The Messenger of Allah called him and killed him between two stones. (c) From this hadith, it is understood that even if he strikes with a heavy stone, intentional murder is established. Intentional murder incurs sin; its proof is in this verse: 'And whoever kills a believer intentionally, his recompense is Hell, abiding eternally therein, and Allah has become angry with him and has cursed him and has prepared for him a great punishment.' (d) (Surah an-Nisa 4:93) And in the hadith: 'Abdullah said: A man said: O Messenger of Allah, which sin is greatest before Allah? He said: That you call upon a rival to Allah while He created you. He said: Then which? He said: Then that you kill your child for fear that he will eat with you.' (e) Footnotes: (a) He said: Everything is error except the sword, and for error there is blood money. (b) He said: No qisas except with iron. (c) Anas ibn Malik said: A woman came out in Madinah wearing ornaments; he said: A Jew struck her with a stone, then the Prophet killed him with two stones. (d) Whoever kills a believer intentionally, his recompense is Hell... (e) Someone (continued on next page).
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi commentary, explaining the essential conditions for intentional murder (qatl al-amd). It opens by stating that dismemberment by sharp instruments necessitates sin and qisas, unless the victim's heirs forgive, and no expiation is due. It then lists two conditions for intentional murder: (1) the striking must be intentional, and (2) the weapon used must be one that ordinarily causes death and dismembers limbs, such as sharp wood or stone. If the weapon is not sharp, intentional murder is not established. The author then presents proofs: a mursal hadith from al-Nu'man ibn Bashir that 'everything is error except the sword,' and another mursal hadith that 'no qisas except with iron.' These are used to argue that only sharp instruments qualify. However, the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) counter that any heavy object that typically causes death, even if not sharp, also establishes intentional murder. They cite the incident of the Jewish man who killed a slave girl with a stone; the Prophet took qisas, showing that a heavy stone qualifies. The passage then provides additional evidence: the Quranic verse on intentional killing (4:93) showing it incurs sin, and a hadith listing major sins. The commentary underscores the intra-Hanafi disagreement on what constitutes a lethal weapon for intentional murder.

Key Terms
قتل عمد (qatl al-amd): Intentional murder, defined by deliberate intent and use of a typically lethal weapon.
قصاص (qisas): Retributive justice, specifically the death penalty for intentional murder, subject to the victim's heirs' pardon.
دية (diyah): Blood money compensation paid for homicide that does not meet the strict conditions for qisas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, which of the following would establish qatl al-amd?
A) Striking with a sharp sword.
B) Striking with a heavy non-sharp stone.
C) Poisoning.
D) Both A and B.

Key Takeaway
The core condition for qatl al-amd is the use of a weapon that ordinarily causes death, but the intra-Hanafi dispute focuses on whether sharpness is required or any heavy lethal object suffices, affecting the application of qisas versus diyah.

Qisas — Retaliation
intermediate
6 min
Rulings of Intentional Murder: Qisas, Pardon, and Expiation
Explains legal consequences of qatl al-amd: qisas, pardon, and no kaffarah, with Shafi'i opposition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on intentional murder regarding qisas, pardon, and kaffarah, and explain why no kaffarah is required, refuting the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Intentional murder requires qisas or pardon; no expiation is due because the Quran does not command it.

In this passage, we explore the legal consequences of intentional murder (qatl al-amd) in Hanafi fiqh. The key rulings are: qisas is obligatory upon the killer, the victim's heirs can pardon and thus waive qisas, and no expiation (kaffarah) is required. The text also presents and refutes the Shafi'i argument that kaffarah should be required by analogy with accidental murder. We will examine the scriptural proofs and understand the Hanafi principle that qiyas cannot override the explicit silence of the Quran.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling on intentional murder
Identify the three key components: qisas is wajib, heirs can pardon, no kaffarah is due.
The act itself is haram.
2
Locate the dalil for qisas and pardon
Examine Quran 2:178, which prescribes qisas and mentions forgiveness. The imperative 'kutiba' indicates obligation.
The hadith of the Jew also supports qisas.
3
Locate the dalil for no kaffarah
Notice that Quran 4:93, which discusses intentional murder, does not mention expiation, whereas Quran 4:92 explicitly prescribes kaffarah for accidental murder. The absence of a textual command is the proof.
4
Analyze the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i argues by qiyas: since accidental murder requires kaffarah due to taking a life, intentional murder is more serious and a fortiori requires kaffarah.
This is a qiyas argument based on the common illa of killing.
5
Understand the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that qiyas cannot override the silence of the nass. Since the Quran does not command kaffarah for intentional murder, it is not required. The text is the limit.
This illustrates the Hanafi usul principle that where the nass is silent, qiyas is not permitted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشرح الثميرى الجزء الثالث) ۲۸۹ كتاب الجنايات ) يعفو الاولياء ولا كفارة فيه [۲۲۹۶ (۳) وشبه العمد عند ابي حنيفة رحمه الله ان يتعمد الضرب بما ليس بسلاح ولا ما اجرى مجراه وقالا رحمهما الله اذا ضربه بحجر عظيم ( بخاری شریف، باب قول الله تعالى ومن يقل مؤمنا متعمد انجز اءه جهنم ص ۱۰۱۴ نمبر ۶ ۶۸) اور عمد کا بدلہ قصاص ہے۔ اس کی دلیل اوپر کی آیت۔ يا ايها الذين آمنوا كتب عليكم القصاص في القتلى الحر بالحر والعبد بالعبد والانثى بالانثى فمن عفى له من اخيه شيء فاتباع بالمعروف (الف) (آیت ۷۸ اسورۃ البقرۃ ) اس آیت سے اس بات کا پتا چلا کہ قتل عمد کا بدلہ قصاص ہے۔ اور یہ بھی پتا چلا کہ اولیاء معاف کرنا چاہے تو معاف کر سکتے ہیں (۲) او پر یہودی والی حدیث بھی گزری کہ باندی کو پتھر سے مارنے کی وجہ سے قصاص کے طور پر یہودی کا سر کچلا گیا۔ قتل عمد میں کفارہ نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ قتل عمد کے تذکرے کے وقت قرآن میں کفارہ کا تذکرہ نہیں ہے۔ آیت یہ ہے۔ ومن يقتل مؤمنا متعمدا فجزاؤه جهنم خالدا فيها وغضب الله عليه ولعنه واعد له عذابا عظيما (ب) (آیت ۹۳ سورۃ النساء۴) اس میں مومن کے قتل عمر میں عذاب کا تذکرہ ہے اور پہلی آیت میں قصاص کا تذکرہ تھا۔ اس لئے اس میں کفارہ لازم نہیں ہو گا ۔ البتہ قتل خطا میں کفارہ لازم ہوگا۔ فائنده امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ جس طرح قتل خطا میں کفارہ لازم ہوتا ہے قتل عمد میں بھی کفارہ لازم ہوگا۔ کیونکہ قتل عمد قتل خطا سے عظیم ہے۔
Al-Sharh al-Thamiri, Part Three, page 289, Kitab al-Jinayat. The heir forgives and there is no expiation in it. [2296 (3)] And shibh al-amd according to Abu Hanifa is that he intentionally strikes with something that is not a weapon nor equivalent. And the two (Sahibayn) said: if he strikes with a great stone... (Bukhari, chapter on the saying of Allah: 'And whoever kills a believer intentionally, his recompense is Hell' p. 1014 no. 68) And the recompense for amd is qisas. Its proof is the verse: 'O you who have believed, prescribed for you is qisas concerning the killed: free for free, slave for slave, female for female. But whoever is forgiven something by his brother, then follow-up with goodness.' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:178) From this verse it becomes clear that the recompense for intentional murder is qisas, and also that the heirs can forgive if they wish. (2) And the hadith about the Jew also passed, that because he struck the slave girl with a stone, the Jew's head was crushed as qisas. There is no expiation in intentional murder, because at the mention of intentional murder in the Qur'an, expiation is not mentioned. That verse is: 'And whoever kills a believer intentionally, his recompense is Hell, abiding eternally therein, and Allah has become angry with him and has cursed him and has prepared for him a great punishment.' (Surah an-Nisa 4:93) In it, punishment is mentioned for intentional murder of a believer, and in the first verse, qisas was mentioned. Therefore, expiation is not wajib in it. But in accidental murder, expiation is wajib. Benefit: Imam Shafi'i says: just as expiation is wajib in accidental murder, so too expiation is wajib in intentional murder, because intentional murder is greater than accidental murder.
Source pages p. 294

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, continuing the discussion of intentional murder (qatl al-amd). It confirms that the victim's heirs can forgive the killer, and that no kaffarah (expiation) is due for intentional murder. The proof for qisas is Quran 2:178, which prescribes retribution and mentions forgiveness. The proof for no kaffarah is that Quran 4:93, which describes intentional murder, mentions only punishment in the Hereafter and does not prescribe expiation. This contrasts with accidental murder (qatl al-khata), where expiation is required (see Quran 4:92). The passage then notes the Shafi'i opinion: if expiation is required for accidental murder, it should a fortiori be required for intentional murder, which is more serious. The Hanafi counterargument is silence of the text; since the Quran does not mention kaffarah for intentional murder, it is not required. This illustrates the Hanafi principle of avoiding qiyas where the explicit text (nass) limits the ruling.

Key Terms
كفارة (kaffarah): Expiation, a religious penalty for certain sins, e.g., freeing a slave or fasting. Here discussed for homicide.
عفو ('afw): Pardon by the victim's heirs, which can waive qisas and allow diyah or forgiveness.
قصاص (qisas): Retributive justice, equivalent to the crime; here, execution for intentional murder.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do Hanafis hold that no expiation (kaffarah) is required for intentional murder?
A) Because the Quran explicitly says so
B) Because intentional murder is less serious than accidental
C) Because the Quran mentions expiation for accidental murder but not for intentional
D) Because the Prophet said so in a hadith

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, intentional murder requires either qisas or pardon; no expiation is required because the Quran does not command it.

Qisas — Retaliation
intermediate
8 min
Shibh 'Amd: Definition, Ruling, and Evidence
Defines shibh 'amd and its ruling with scriptural proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of shibh 'amd, identify its three consequences (sin, kaffarah, heavy diyah), and explain the scriptural proofs for each.

Core Idea
Shibh 'amd: intentional strike with a non-lethal tool – no qisas, but heavy diyah on the 'aqilah.

Not all intentional killings are equal under Hanafi law. When a person strikes another with an instrument that does not usually kill – like a stick or whip – but death results, the law classifies this as shibh 'amd (semi-intentional). This category bridges intentional and accidental homicide, carrying its own unique consequences: sin, expiation, and heavy blood money paid by the killer's clan. The passage before you defines this category and anchors it in Quranic verses, prophetic hadith, and the practice of the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
First, pinpoint the definition of shibh ‘amd: striking intentionally with an instrument not typically lethal. Then list the three consequences explicitly stated in the passage: sin (ithm), expiation (kaffarah), and heavy blood money (diyah mughallazah) on the ‘aqilah, with no retaliatory execution (qisas).
Contrast this with ‘amd (lethal weapon, qisas applies) and khata’ (accidental, no sin).
2
Locate the scriptural proofs
The passage cites three distinct proofs: (1) Quran 4:93 for the sin of intentional killing, applied here because the strike is intended; (2) Quran 4:92 for kaffarah and diyah, originally for khata’ but extended via qiyas; (3) the hadith of the two women from Hudhayl for the liability of the ‘aqilah. Identify each proof in the source.
The hadith establishes diyah on the ‘aqilah for the woman killed by a stone – a case analogous to shibh ‘amd.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how each proof yields the ruling. For Quran 4:93, the phrase 'manslaughter intentionally' includes shibh ‘amd because the striker intended the blow. For Quran 4:92, the obligation of kaffarah and diyah in khata’ is extended to shibh ‘amd by qiyas, since both involve death without fully lethal intent. The hadith shows that diyah is on the ‘aqilah, preventing the killer from bearing it alone.
The Hanafi school uses qiyas to apply the khata’ verses to shibh ‘amd, as both lack intent to kill.
4
Note the cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
Recognize that some schools (e.g., Shafi‘i) may classify such killings as ‘amd (intentional) because the blow was intended, and thus qisas would apply. The Hanafi school distinguishes based on the typical lethality of the instrument.
The difference stems from whether intent to strike is equated with intent to kill.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position relies on the authority of the Quranic text, the practice of the Companions (athar of ‘Ali and ‘Abdullah), and the hadith on ‘aqilah. It is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position due to its strong evidentiary basis and consistency with the principles of gradualism in punishment.
Heavy diyah (100 camels) divided into four categories of 25 each is fixed by the athar of ‘Abdullah ibn Mas‘ud, as cited in the passage.

مغلظہ کیا ہے۔
Or with a large piece of wood, it is intentional. And shibh 'amd is that he intentionally strikes him with what does not usually kill. [229?] (4) Its consequence according to the two statements is sin and kaffarah, and no qisas in it, and in it is heavy diyah on the 'aqilah. That from which death does not normally occur, he deliberately kills, like striking with a stick and he died, so this is shibh 'amd. In this, diyah, kaffarah, and sin are obligatory; qisas and retaliation are not obligatory. The hadith about the slave girl has passed, that a Jew crushed her head with a stone and the Prophet undertook qisas. There is an athar: 'Ali said: The killed one by whip and stick is shibh 'amd. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah...). From this athar it became known that striking with something that generally does not kill a person, like a stick etc., then this killing is shibh 'amd. [2297] (4) On both statements, its punishment is sin and kaffarah. No qisas in it, rather heavy diyah on the 'aqilah. In whatever manner shibh 'amd is established, its punishment is a great sin. Second, kaffarah becomes obligatory: freeing a believing slave or slave girl. Third, heavy diyah becomes obligatory on his 'aqilah. The proof for sin has passed: 'And whoever kills a believer intentionally, his recompense is Hell, abiding therein, and Allah's wrath and curse are upon him, and He has prepared for him a great punishment.' (Surah al-Nisa 4:93). Since this killing is also intentional, therefore according to the verse, there is great sin. And the proof for kaffarah is this verse: 'And whoever kills a believer by mistake, then freeing a believing slave and blood money delivered to his family unless they remit.' (Surah al-Nisa 4:92). From this verse it became known that in killing by mistake, kaffarah and diyah are obligatory. As for kaffarah, it is freeing a believing slave, and if not found, then fasting two consecutive months. And diyah on the 'aqilah; its proof is this hadith: Abu Hurairah said: Two women from Hudhayl fought, one threw a stone at the other and killed her and what was in her womb, so they brought the case to the Prophet, and he ruled that the diyah of her fetus is a slave or a slave girl, and he ruled that the diyah of the woman is on her 'aqilah. (Bukhari, Muslim). From this hadith it became known that diyah is obligatory on the killer's 'aqilah. The paternal relatives of the killer are called 'aqilah. Since they did not prevent the killer from killing, therefore it becomes obligatory on them to pay within three years. Footnotes: (a) 'Ali said: The killed by whip and stick is shibh 'amd. (b) Someone killed a believer by mistake, so he frees a believing slave and hands over the diyah to his heirs unless they forgive. (c) Abu Hurairah says: Two women from tribe Hudhayl fought... [repeated]. 'Aqilah: the family of a person, the people of his profession are called 'aqilah who bear the diyah. The number of diyah is: one hundred camels or one thousand dinars or ten thousand dirhams or two hundred cows. In shibh 'amd, twenty-five hiqqah, twenty-five jadha'ah, twenty-five bint labun, and twenty-five bint makhad are obligatory as diyah. The proof is this athar: 'Abdullah said regarding shibh 'amd: twenty-five hiqqah, twenty-five jadha'ah, twenty-five bint labun, and twenty-five bint makhad. (Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi). This is heavy diyah. And the proof for heavy diyah is this athar: 'Uthman ibn 'Affan and Zayd ibn Thabit said regarding the heavy [diyah]: forty jadha'ah khalifah, thirty hiqqah, and thirty bint labun; and in mistake: thirty hiqqah, thirty bint labun, twenty bani labun male, and twenty bint makhad. (Abu Dawud). In this athar, it is stated what heavy diyah is.
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage defines and provides evidence for shibh 'amd (semi-intentional homicide) according to the Hanafi school. The key elements are: (1) The killer intentionally strikes the victim but with an instrument that does not usually cause death (e.g., a stick or whip). (2) The legal consequences are threefold: great sin (because intent to harm is present), kaffarah (expiation by freeing a believing slave or fasting two months), and heavy diyah (blood money) paid by the 'aqilah (paternal relatives) over three years. (3) No qisas (retaliatory execution) applies because the weapon is not typically lethal. The passage cites Quranic verses (4:93 for sin, 4:92 for kaffarah/diyah) and hadith (the two women of Hudhayl, and athar from 'Ali, 'Abdullah, 'Uthman, and Zayd) to support these rulings. It also specifies the composition of the heavy diyah (100 camels or equivalent) and the lighter diyah for khata' (mistake) as a contrast. The commentary explains that the 'aqilah's liability stems from their failure to prevent the killer from committing the act. Students should note that shibh 'amd is distinct from both 'amd (intentional with lethal weapon, which carries qisas) and khata' (mistake, which has no sin but still requires kaffarah and diyah).

Key Terms
شبه العمد (shibh al-‘amd): Intentional striking with an instrument that does not usually kill, resulting in death (e.g., stick, whip). It is distinct from ‘amd (lethal instrument) and khata’ (accidental).
عاقلة (‘āqilah): The paternal relatives (and sometimes professional guild) of the killer who pay the diyah collectively over three years, because they failed to prevent the homicide.
دية مغلظة (diyah mughallaẓah): Heavy blood money: 100 camels (or equivalent) paid over three years, specified in composition as 25 each of hiqqah, jadha‘ah, bint labun, and bint makhad for shibh ‘amd.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is a consequence of shibh 'amd?
A) The killer must be executed (qisas)
B) The killer must pay blood money (diyah) from his own wealth only
C) The killer's 'aqilah must pay heavy diyah, and the killer must perform kaffarah
D) The killer is free from all punishment because the instrument was non-lethal

Key Takeaway
Shibh 'amd is a distinct Hanafi category of homicide with sin, kaffarah, and heavy diyah on the 'aqilah, but no qisas, rooted in the typical lethality of the instrument.

Qisas — Retaliation
intermediate

Khata' (Manslaughter): Types and Ruling
Describes two types of manslaughter and their ruling with evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two types of khata', explain why there is no sin, and derive the obligations of kaffarah and diyah from the evidence.

Core Idea
Accidental killing is sinless but incurs kaffarah and diyah on the 'aqilah.

In Islamic law, not all homicides are equal. This passage distinguishes two forms of manslaughter (khata') and clarifies that while the killer bears no sin due to lack of intent, he must still expiate and compensate the victim's family. The ruling is anchored in the Quranic verse 4:92 and the practice of the Companions, establishing a comprehensive framework for accidental killing.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of khata'
Read the passage to distinguish khata' fi al-qasd (mistake in intent) from khata' fi al-fi'l (mistake in action). Note the difference in the intended target.
The key is that in both, the killer did not intend to kill a human.
2
State the ruling: no sin but obligations
The passage explicitly says 'la ma'tham fih' (no sin in it). Why? Because intent is lacking. However, two obligations arise: kaffarah (expiation) and diyah (blood money) paid by the 'aqilah.
Kaffarah is an act of worship; diyah is financial compensation.
3
Analyze the primary evidence from Quran 4:92
The verse commands freeing a believing slave and delivering diyah for accidental killing. Identify the words 'khata'an' and understand that the imperative (fatahrir) indicates obligation (wujub) in Hanafi usul.
The verse directly supports both kaffarah and diyah.
4
Examine the athar evidence for diyah composition
The passage cites reports from 'Abdullah (Ibn Mas'ud) and 'Uthman/Zayd detailing the number and ages of camels for khata' diyah. This is the standard composition in the Hanafi school.
The diyah for khata' is lighter than that for shibh 'amd.
5
Understand the role of the 'aqilah
The 'aqilah (paternal relatives or professional guild) bear the diyah over three years, as they are considered responsible for the killer's negligence.
This spreads the financial burden and reflects communal responsibility.

[2298] (5) Khata' is of two types: mistake in intent - that he shoots a person thinking he is game, but it turns out to be a human; [2299] (6) and mistake in act - that he shoots a target and it hits a human. [2300] (7) And its consequence is kaffarah and diyah on the 'aqilah, and no sin in it. 'Aqilah: the family of a person, the people of his profession are called 'aqilah who bear the diyah. The number of diyah is: one hundred camels or one thousand dinars or ten thousand dirhams or two hundred cows. In shibh 'amd, twenty-five hiqqah, twenty-five jadha'ah, twenty-five bint labun, and twenty-five bint makhad are obligatory as diyah. The proof is this athar: 'Abdullah said regarding shibh 'amd: twenty-five hiqqah, twenty-five jadha'ah, twenty-five bint labun, and twenty-five bint makhad. (Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi). This is heavy diyah. And the proof for heavy diyah is this athar: 'Uthman ibn 'Affan and Zayd ibn Thabit said regarding the heavy [diyah]: forty jadha'ah khalifah, thirty hiqqah, and thirty bint labun; and in mistake: thirty hiqqah, thirty bint labun, twenty bani labun male, and twenty bint makhad. (Abu Dawud). In this athar, it is stated what heavy diyah is. The reason there is no sin is because he did not intentionally kill, rather killed by mistake, therefore there will be no sin. And kaffarah is required; its proof is this verse: 'And whoever kills a believer by mistake, then freeing a believing slave and blood money delivered to his family unless they remit.' (Surah al-Nisa 4:92). In this verse, footnotes: (a) 'Abdullah said regarding shibh 'amd: twenty-five hiqqah, twenty-five jadha'ah, twenty-five bint labun, and twenty-five bint makhad. (b) Zayd ibn Thabit said regarding the heavy diyah: forty jadha'ah khalifah, thirty hiqqah, thirty bint labun; and in khata': thirty hiqqah, thirty bint labun, twenty bani labun male, and twenty bint makhad. (c) 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-Aziz wrote regarding khata': that he intends to hit one person but hits another. (d) Someone killed a believer by mistake, so he frees a believing slave and hands over the diyah to his heirs unless they forgive.
Source pages p. 296

Commentary
This passage defines khata' (manslaughter by mistake) as having two forms: (1) mistake in intention (khata' fi al-qasd) – when one intends to hit a permissible target (like game) but accidentally hits a human; (2) mistake in action (khata' fi al-fi'l) – when one intends to hit an inanimate target but the projectile strikes a human. The ruling is that there is no sin because there was no intent to kill a human; however, kaffarah (expiation) and diyah (blood money) are obligatory. The diyah is paid by the 'aqilah (paternal relatives or professional guild) over three years. The passage also clarifies the composition of diyah: for khata', it is 30 hiqqah, 30 bint labun, 20 male bani labun, and 20 bint makhad (lighter than heavy diyah for shibh 'amd). The primary evidence is Quran 4:92, which mandates kaffarah and diyah for accidental killing. The 'aqilah's liability is explained as stemming from their failure to prevent the killer from acting negligently. Students should note that khata' is distinct from shibh 'amd (which has sin) and 'amd (which has qisas).

Key Terms
خطأ في القصد (khaṭa’ fī al-qaṣd): Mistake in intent: the killer intends to hit a permissible target (e.g., a game animal) but accidentally hits a human. The action is intentional toward the target, but the outcome is unintended.
خطأ في الفعل (khaṭa’ fī al-fi‘l): Mistake in action: the killer aims at an inanimate target (e.g., shooting at a target) but misses and hits a human. The intent was lawful, but the execution fails.
كفارة (kaffārah): Expiation for accidental killing: freeing a believing slave, or if unable, fasting two consecutive months (as derived from other verses). This is an act of worship to atone for the loss of life.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is an example of khata' fi al-qasd (mistake in intent)?
A) A hunter shoots at a deer but hits a person hiding in the bushes
B) A man shoots at a target and the arrow ricochets and kills a bystander
C) A person intentionally strikes another with a stick and the victim dies
D) A driver accidentally runs over a pedestrian while texting

Key Takeaway
Khata' has no sin but requires kaffarah and diyah, with the diyah borne by the 'aqilah, as per Quran 4:92 and Companion practice.

Qisas — Retaliation

6 min
Obligation of Qisas for Intentional Murder of a Protected Life
Stating the ruling that qisas is obligatory for intentional murder of a protected life

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that qisas is wajib for intentional murder of a protected life and identify the Quranic proof.

Core Idea
Qisas is wajib perpetually for intentional murder of a life protected by law.

In this lesson, we examine a foundational ruling of Islamic criminal law: the obligation of qisas (retributive execution) for intentional murder of a person whose blood is inviolable. The passage from Al-Sharh al-Sameri clearly states the ruling and provides the primary textual evidence from the Quran and Sunnah. Understanding this ruling is essential to grasp the Hanafi approach to justice and the rights of victims' families.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The passage states that qisas is obligatory (wajib) for killing someone who is 'protected life' (mahqun al-dam) when the killing is intentional.
The ruling applies only to intentional murder, not accidental.
2
Define 'protected life' (mahqun al-dam)
Protected means the person's blood is inviolable – it is not lawful to kill them. The text mentions exceptions: apostates, married adulterers, and intentional murderers.
Muslims and dhimmis are protected unless they fall under these exceptions.
3
Note the perpetual nature of the obligation
The phrase 'ala al-ta'bid' means the obligation does not expire; qisas remains enforceable until executed or pardoned.
The heira can always demand qisas or pardon.
4
Cite the primary proof from Quran
The verse (al-Ma'idah 5:45) states 'a life for a life', which is a clear command indicating obligation.
This is a qat'i (definitive) text in transmission and meaning.
5
Recognize the option of pardon
The hadith from Abu Huraira gives the heira a choice between executing the killer or pardoning him. Qisas is not automatic.
Pardon can be for free or with diyah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[2304] (11) والقصاص واجب بقتل كل محقون الدم على التابيد اذا قتل عمدا.

قصاص واجب ہوتا ہے ہمیشہ کے طور پر محفوظ الدم کو قتل کرنے سے جبکہ جان بوجھ کر قتل کرے۔ ایسا آدمی جس کا خون مرتد ہونے یا زنا کرنے یا کسی کو قتل کرنے سے مباح الدم نہ ہو اور ہمیشہ کے طور پر اس کا خون محفوظ ہو اس کو جان بوجھ کر کوئی قتل کرے تو اس قتل کرنے پر قصاص واجب ہوتا ہے۔ یعنی جیسا اس نے قتل کیا قاتل کو بھی قتل کر دیا جائے گا۔ قصاص واجب ہونے کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے۔ و كتبنا عليهم فيها ان النفس بالنفس والعين بالعين والانف بالانف والاذن بالاذن والسن بالسن والجروح قصاص فمن تصدق به فهو كفارة له (ج) ( آیت 45 سورۃ المائدۃ 5) یہ حدیث بھی ہے۔ (2)حدثني ابو هريرة قال لما فتح على رسول الله مكة قام في الناس فحمد الله واثنى عليه ثم قال ومن قتل له قتيل فهو بخير النظرين اما ان يعفو واما ان يقتل (د) (ترندى شریف، باب ما جاء فی حکم ولی التقتيل في القصاص والعفوص ص 260 نمبر 1405)
[2304] (11) And qisas is obligatory for killing every protected life perpetually when one kills intentionally.

Qisas is obligatory perpetually for killing a protected life, when one kills intentionally. A person whose blood is not lawful to shed due to apostasy, adultery, or killing someone else, and his blood is perpetually protected, then if someone kills him intentionally, qisas becomes obligatory for that killing. That is, as he killed, the killer will also be killed. The proof for the obligation of qisas is this verse: 'And We prescribed for them therein: a life for a life, an eye for an eye, a nose for a nose, an ear for an ear, a tooth for a tooth, and for wounds is legal retribution. But whoever gives it up as charity, it shall be an expiation for him.' (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:45). Also this hadith: Abu Huraira narrated: 'When Mecca was conquered for the Messenger of Allah, he stood among the people, praised Allah, and said: Whoever has a relative killed, he has two choices: either to pardon or to kill.' (Sunan al-Tirmidhi, Book of Ruling on Wali in Qisas and Pardon, p260 no.1405)
Source pages p. 298

Commentary
This passage establishes the principle that qisas (retributive execution) is wajib (obligatory) for intentional murder of a person whose blood is protected (mahqun al-dam). Such a person is one who is not lawful to kill due to apostasy, adultery, or murder (i.e., not a mubah al-dam). The obligation is perpetual (ala al-ta'bid), meaning it does not lapse. The verse from Surah al-Ma'idah (5:45) is cited as primary evidence, which clearly prescribes qisas. The hadith from Abu Huraira gives the heir of the victim a choice between execution or pardon. The Hanafi school understands that the default obligation is qisas, but the heir may pardon or accept diyah. The text emphasizes that the victim must be a 'protected life' meaning a Muslim or a dhimmi whose life is inviolable. The obligation is upon the killer, and the state implements it upon the request of the victim's heirs.

Key Terms
محقون الدم (mahqun al-dam): A person whose blood is protected and inviolable, i.e., it is not lawful to kill them. This includes Muslims and dhimmis, excluding apostates, married adulterers, and intentional murderers.
قصاص (qisas): Retributive punishment where the offender is subjected to the same harm as inflicted on the victim, specifically execution for intentional murder.
على التابيد (ala al-ta'bid): Perpetually, meaning the obligation of qisas does not expire with time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following persons is NOT considered mahqun al-dam?
A) A Muslim who has never committed a crime.
B) A dhimmi living under Islamic rule.
C) A person who has committed murder with intent.
D) A person who has apostatized from Islam.

Key Takeaway
Qisas is wajib for intentional murder of a protected life, but the heirs retain the right to pardon or demand execution.

Qisas — Retaliation
beginner
6 min
Obligation of Qisas for Intentional Killing of a Protected Person
Ruling and proof: qisas is wajib for intentional murder of a protected person

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that qisas is wajib for intentional murder of a protected person and identify the Quranic and Hadith proofs that establish it.

Core Idea
Qisas is wajib for intentional murder of a protected person; the victim's family may choose forgiveness.

This lesson examines the obligation of qisas (retaliation) for intentional murder of a person whose blood is inviolable (mahqun al-dam). The author of the matn rules that qisas is wajib perpetually, and provides two primary proofs: a Quranic verse and a Prophetic hadith. Understanding this ruling requires recognizing both the conditions for qisas and the options available to the victim's heirs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is intentional killing of a protected person. The ruling is that qisas is wajib (obligatory) perpetually (ala al-ta'bid).
The term 'protected person' is key — those whose blood is inviolable.
2
Define 'protected person' (mahqun al-dam)
Protected persons include Muslims and dhimmis who have not committed crimes that make their blood lawful: apostasy, zina (for muhsan), or murder. The victim must be free from these conditions.
The text explicitly excludes apostates, adulterers, and murderers from protection.
3
Locate the proofs (dalil)
The author cites two proofs: Quran 5:45 ('life for life...') and a hadith from the conquest of Mecca where the Prophet gave the victim's family the choice between forgiveness and execution.
The Quranic proof is qat'i al-thubut (certain transmission) but zanni al-dalala (its implication for wujub is open to interpretation).
4
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah (point of evidence)
The verse uses 'kutiba' (written/prescribed) which in Hanafi usul indicates wujub. The hadith confirms that the option to kill (i.e., qisas) is a legal right of the heirs.
The imperative form in the verse and the explicit option in the hadith together establish the obligation.
5
Note the option of forgiveness
The ruling is not automatic enforcement; the victim's heirs may waive qisas. This differentiates wujub from fard — wujib can be waived by human right.
If the heirs forgive, the killer may still be liable for diyah (blood money) unless explicitly waived.

Source Text

ایسا آدمی جس کا خون مرتد ہونے یا زنا کرنے یا کسی کو قتل کرنے سے مباح الد م نہ ہو اور ہمیشہ کے طور پر اس کا خون محفوظ ہو اس کو جان بوجھ کر کوئی قتل کرے تو اس قتل کرنے پر قصاص واجب ہوتا ہے۔ یعنی جیسا اس نے قتل کیا قاتل کو بھی قتل کر دیا جائے گا۔ قصاص واجب ہونے کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے۔ و كتبنا عليهم فيها ان النفس بالنفس والعين بالعين والانف بالانف والاذن بالاذن والسن بالسن والجروح قصاص فمن تصدق به فهو كفارة له (ج) ( آیت ۴۵ سورۃ المائدۃ ۵) یہ حدیث بھی ہے۔ (۲) حدثني ابو هريرة قال لما فتح على رسول الله مكة قام في الناس فحمد الله واثنى عليه ثم قال ومن قتل له قتيل فهو بخير النظرين اما ان يعفو واما ان يقتل (د) (ترندى شریف، باب ما جاء فی حکم ولی التقتيل في القصاص والعفوص ۲۶۰ نمبر ۱۴۰۵)

[2304] (11) And qisas is obligatory by killing every protected-blood person perpetually when he kills intentionally.

A person whose blood is not rendered lawful by becoming an apostate or committing zina or killing someone, and his blood is permanently protected—if someone kills him intentionally, then qisas is obligatory upon that killing. That is, just as he killed, the killer will also be killed. The proof for qisas being obligatory is this verse: 'And We prescribed for them therein that life for life, eye for eye, nose for nose, ear for ear, tooth for tooth, and wounds equal for equal. But whoever gives it up as charity, it will be an expiation for him.' (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:45) And there is also this hadith: Abu Huraira reported: When Allah's Messenger conquered Mecca, he stood among the people, praised Allah and then said, 'Whoever has had a relative killed, he has two options: either to forgive or to kill.' (Tirmidhi, no. 1405)

Footnote: (from previous page) Forgiven; the one who dies in an ear is forgiven?; and in the treasure chest the fifth share? (a) Ibrahim said: Whoever digs in other than his building or builds in other than his sky, then he is liable. (b) Ibrahim said: Whoever digs in other than his building or builds in other than his property, then he is liable. (c) We prescribed for them that life for life, eye for eye, nose for nose, ear for ear, tooth for tooth, and wounds equal for equal; and whoever gives it up as charity, it is an expiation for him. (d) When the Prophet conquered Mecca, he praised Allah and then said: Whoever has had a relative killed, he has two options: to forgive or to kill.
Source pages p. 298

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof establishing the obligation of qisas (retaliation) for intentional murder of a protected person (mahqun al-dam). The author specifies that qisas is wajib perpetually (ala al-ta'bid) when a person whose blood is inviolable is killed intentionally. Protected persons are those who are not apostates, adulterers (muhsan), or murderers themselves—individuals whose blood is not rendered lawful by such crimes. The proof includes the Quranic verse (5:45) which establishes retaliation for life and limb, and a hadith from the conquest of Mecca where the Prophet gave the victim's family the choice between forgiveness and execution. The footnote adds more details from earlier discussions and repeats the athar from Ibrahim.

Key Terms
محقون الدم (mahqūn al-dam): A person whose blood is inviolable (protected) and cannot be lawfully shed.
قصاص (qisās): Retaliation in kind for murder or bodily harm; the punishment of the offender exactly as he caused harm.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Qisas — Retaliation

Equality in Qisas: Free, Slave, Muslim, and Dhimmi
Ruling on qisas across categories with inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on qisas across free/slave and Muslim/dhimmi categories and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the hadith and Quranic evidence.

Core Idea
A free person is executed for killing a slave in Hanafi qisas; the hadith overrides the apparent limitation of the verse.

In this passage, the author presents the Hanafi ruling that qisas applies equally across free, slave, Muslim, and dhimmi. This position is disputed by Imam al-Shafi'i, who restricts qisas to same categories. The passage provides key proofs from the Quran and hadith, and we will analyze the reasoning behind each school's argument.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: a free person is killed for a slave, and a Muslim is killed for a dhimmi. Note that the text also covers free for free, slave for free, etc.
This is the established Hanafi view (zahir al-riwayah).
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that a free person is not killed for a slave. Recognise the opposing school.
The Shafi'i school relies on the apparent meaning of Quran 2:178.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the verse: 'the free for the free, the slave for the slave.' Understand how it is used to argue for same-category qisas.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafis cite the hadith 'Whoever kills his slave, we will kill him' and the general principle of equality in hurmah (inviolability). The hadith overrides the apparent limitation.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but is accepted as proof due to its explicit wording.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafis execute a free man for killing a slave; Shafi'is require only diyah (blood money).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۳۰۵] (١٢) ويقتل الحر بالحر والحر بالعبدوالعبد بالحر والعبد بالعبد والمسلم 

اس آیت اور حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ قتل عمد میں قصاص لازم ہے۔ البتہ ولی کو معاف کرنے کا حق ہے۔ یہ تین آدمی محفوظ الدم نہیں ہے زانی، مرتد اور قاتل۔ حدیث میں ہے۔ عن عبد الله بن مسعود قال قال رسول الله الا الله لا يحل دم امرئ مسلم يشهد ان لا اله الا الله وانى رسول الله الا باحدى ثلاث الثيب الزانى والنفس بالنفس والتارك لدينه المفارق للجماعة (الف) ( ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء لاتحل دم امرا مسلم الا باحدی ثلاث ص ۲۵۹ نمبر ۱۴۳۰۲ر مسلم شریف، باب ما یباح به دم المسلم ص ۵۹ نمبر ۱۶۷۶) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ مرتد ، زانی اور قاتل کا خون محفوظ نہیں ہے۔ اس کے علاوہ کا خون محفوظ ہے۔ اس لئے اس کو قتل کرنے سے قصاص لازم ہوگا ۔ [۲۳۰۵) (۱۲) قتل کیا جائے گا آزاد آزاد کے بدلے اور آزاد غلام کے بدلے اور غلام آزاد کے بدلے اور غلام غلام کے بدلے اور مسلمان ذمی
کے بدلے۔ آزاد آدمی آزاد آدمی کو قتل کر دے چاہے وہ مرد ہو یا عورت، قاتل کو قصاص میں قتل کیا جائے گا۔ اور آزاد آدمی کسی دوسرے کے غلام کو قتل کر دے تو غلام کے بدلے آزاد آدمی قتل کیا جائے گا۔ اور مسلمان نے ذمی کافر کوقتل کر دیا تو ذمی کے بدلے مسلمان قتل کیا جائے گا۔ آیت میں ہے۔ یا ایها الذين آمنوا كتب عليكم القصاص في القتلى الحر بالحر والعبد بالعبد والانثى بالابثي فمن عفى له من اخيه شيء فاتباع بالمعروف واداء اليه باحسان (ب) (آیت ۷۸ اسورۃ البقرۃ ۲) اس آیت سے معلوم ہوا کہ آزاد آزاد کے بدلے اور غلام غلام کے بدلے قتل کیا جائے گا۔ اور آزاد مرد ہو یا عورت دونوں شامل ہیں (۲) حدیث گزر چکی ہے کہ ایک باندی کے بدلے یہودی کو پھر سے کچل کر مارا جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ عورت کے بدلے مرد کوقتل کیا جائے گا۔ ( بخاری شریف، باب اذ اقتل بحجر او بعصاص ۱۰۱۶ نمبر ۶۸۷۷) اور غلام کے بدلے آزاد کو قتل کیا جائے گا اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن سمرة بن جندب قال قال رسول الله له من قتل عبده قتلناه ومن جدع عبده جدعناه (ج) (ترندی شریف ، باب ماجاء فی الرجل يقتل عبده ص ۲۶۱ نمبر ۱۳۱۴ را ابن ماجه شریف، باب هل يقتل الحر بالعبد ص ۳۸۳ نمبر ۲۶۶۳ / ابو داؤد شریف، باب من قتل عبده او مثل به ص ۲۷۲ نمبر ۴۵۱۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ آزاد آدمی غلام کو قتل کر دے تو آزاد کو قتل کیا جائے گا۔ اور غلام آزاد کوقتل کر دے تو غلام بدرجہ اولی قصاص میں قتل کیا جائے گا۔
امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ غلام کے بدلے آزاد نہیں قتل کیا جائے گا۔
حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے فرمایا کسی مسلمان کا خون حلال نہیں ہے جو لا الہ الا اللہ الخ پڑھتا ہو مگر تین طریقوں سے۔ ایک عیب زانی ہو، دوسرا جان جان کے بدلے، تیسرا دین کو چھوڑنے والا جماعت سے دور رہنے والا ( ب) اے ایمان والو تم پر قصاص فرض کیا گیا ہے مقتول کے بارے میں ۔ آزاد آزاد کے بدلے، غلام غلام کے بدلے ہونٹ مؤنث کے بدلے۔ پس اگر کسی نے اپنے بھائی کو معاف کر دیا تو معروف کے ساتھ مانگنا ہے۔ اور اس کی طرف احسان کے ساتھ ادا کرنا ہے ( ج ) آپ نے فرمایا کسی نے اپنا غلام قتل کیا تو میں اس کو قتل کروں گا اور اس کی ناک کاٹی تو میں اس کی ناک کاٹوں گا۔
[2305] (12) And the free is killed for the free, and the free for the slave, and the slave for the free, and the slave for the slave, and the Muslim for the dhimmi.

From this verse and hadith it is known that in intentional killing, qisas is obligatory. However, the guardian (wali) has the right to forgive. These three persons are not mahqun al-dam: the adulterer (thayyib), the apostate, and the murderer. In a hadith: 'Indeed, the blood of a Muslim who testifies that there is no god but Allah and that I am the Messenger of Allah is not lawful except for one of three: the married adulterer, life for life, and the one who leaves his religion and separates from the community.' (Tirmidhi, no. 1430; Muslim, no. 1676) From this hadith it is known that the blood of the apostate, the adulterer, and the killer is not protected. Other than these, the blood is protected. Therefore, killing such a person necessitates qisas.

[2305] (12) The free will be killed in place of the free, and the free in place of the slave, and the slave in place of the free, and the slave in place of the slave, and the Muslim in place of the dhimmi. If a free person kills a free person, whether male or female, the killer will be executed in qisas. And if a free person kills another's slave, then the free person will be executed in place of the slave. And if a Muslim kills a dhimmi disbeliever, then the Muslim will be executed in place of the dhimmi. In the verse: 'O you who have believed, prescribed for you is qisas in cases of murder: the free for the free, the slave for the slave, and the female for the female. But whoever is granted a pardon from his brother, then follow-up with what is appropriate and payment with good conduct.' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:178) From this verse it is known that the free is killed for the free, and the slave for the slave. And the free includes both male and female. (2) The hadith has passed that a Jew was crushed to death in place of a slave girl, from which it is known that a man is killed for a woman. (Bukhari, no. 6877) And for the free being killed for the slave, the proof is this hadith: 'Whoever kills his slave, we will kill him; and whoever mutilates his slave, we will mutilate him.' (Tirmidhi, no. 1314; Ibn Majah, no. 2663; Abu Dawud, no. 4515) From this hadith it is known that if a free person kills a slave, the free will be killed. And if a slave kills a free person, then the slave is killed a fortiori in qisas.

Imam al-Shafi'i says that a free person is not killed for a slave.

Footnote: (a) The Prophet said: The blood of a Muslim who testifies that there is no god but Allah... is not lawful except for three: the married adulterer, life for life, and the one who leaves his religion. (b) O believers, prescribed for you is qisas in cases of murder: the free for the free, the slave for the slave, the female for the female. So if someone is pardoned by his brother, then follow-up with what is appropriate and payment with good conduct. (c) The Prophet said: Whoever kills his slave, we will kill him; whoever mutilates his slave, we will mutilate him.
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding equality in qisas. The Hanafi position is that a free person is executed for killing a slave, and a Muslim is executed for killing a dhimmi (non-Muslim under Muslim protection). The author cites several proofs: the Quranic verse (2:178) mentioning 'free for free, slave for slave' is interpreted by Hanafis to mean that qisas applies across categories, as the general principle is equality of lives. Additionally, the hadith from Samura ibn Jundub states that if a free man kills his slave, the free man is executed, indicating that a free person can be killed for a slave. Another hadith recounts that a Jew was executed for killing a slave girl, showing that a Muslim can be executed for a dhimmi? Actually careful: the hadith about the Jew is mentioned earlier; it shows that a man (presumably free) is killed for a woman (slave). The author also mentions Imam al-Shafi'i's objection: he holds that a free person is not killed for a slave. The Hanafi response relies on the literal wording of the hadith and the general principle of qisas. The text also repeats the hadith about three types of people whose blood is not protected: the married adulterer, the murderer, and the apostate. This underlines who is not a protected person.

Key Terms
ذمي (dhimmi): A non-Muslim subject of an Islamic state who is granted protection of life and property in exchange for jizyah.
محقون الدم (formerly) (mahqūn al-dam): A person whose blood is inviolable and protected from being shed without legal justification.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if a free Muslim kills a dhimmi (non-Muslim citizen) intentionally?
A) The free Muslim is not executed; he only pays diyah
B) The free Muslim is executed in qisas for the dhimmi
C) The free Muslim is executed only if the dhimmi's family pays a fee
D) The free Muslim is not liable because the dhimmi is not a protected person

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, qisas applies across free/slave and Muslim/dhimmi lines based on the hadith 'Whoever kills his slave, we will kill him' and the principle of equal inviolability of all protected life.

Qisas Between Free, Slave, Muslim, and Dhimmi: Hanafi Position and Shafi'i Dispute
Ruling on qisas between free, slave, Muslim, and dhimmi with proofs and Shafi'i dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qisas when the victim is a slave or dhimmi, and identify the opposing Shafi'i position with its proof, evaluating the Hanafi response.

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, a free person is killed for a slave and a Muslim for a dhimmi, based on specific hadiths.

This lesson examines a key dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools over qisas when the victim is a slave or a dhimmi. The Hanafi school affirms qisas in these cases, while the Shafi'i school denies it, leading to different practical outcomes. We will trace the arguments on both sides.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and its proofs
Identify the exact ruling: a free person is killed for a slave, and a Muslim for a dhimmi. Then cite the Quranic verse (2:178) and the hadith of Samurah (free for slave) and Ibn Umar (Muslim for dhimmi).
The Hanafi rely on specific, action-based hadiths.
2
Identify the Shafi'i objection and its proofs
State the Shafi'i position: no qisas for a slave or a dhimmi. Their proofs include the hadith of Ibn Abbas ('لا يقتل حر بعبد') and the hadith of Ali ('لا يقتل مسلم بكافر').
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
See how the Hanafi rebut these proofs: the hadith of Samurah is more specific; the hadith of Ibn Umar involves a direct action of the Prophet which takes precedence over general statements.
The Hanafi response is based on strengthening the specific over the general.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under Hanafi, the killer is executed; under Shafi'i, only diyah (blood money) is due.
This affects actual legal outcomes in applied cases.

Book of Offenses [2305] (12) A free person is killed for a free person, a free person for a slave, a slave for a free person, a slave for a slave, and a Muslim for a dhimmi. From this verse and hadith, it is understood that qisas is obligatory in intentional murder. However, the guardian has the right to forgive. These three persons are not protected blood: the adulterer, the apostate, and the murderer. In a hadith: from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud that the Prophet (saw) said: 'Indeed, the blood of a Muslim who testifies that there is no god but Allah and that I am the Messenger of Allah is not lawful except for one of three: the married adulterer, a life for a life, and the one who abandons his religion and separates from the community.' (Footnotes: references to Tirmidhi and Muslim). From this hadith, it is understood that the blood of an apostate, adulterer, and murderer is not protected. The blood of others is protected. Therefore, killing him necessitates qisas. [2305] (12) A free person is killed for a free person, a free person for a slave, a slave for a free person, a slave for a slave, and a Muslim for a dhimmi. If a free man kills a free man, whether man or woman, the killer is executed in qisas. If a free man kills another's slave, the free man is killed for the slave. If a Muslim kills a dhimmi kafir, the Muslim is killed for the dhimmi. In the verse: 'O you who believe, prescribed for you is qisas regarding the slain: free for free, slave for slave, female for female. But whoever is forgiven something by his brother, then follow-up with what is acceptable and payment with good conduct.' (Verse 178 Surah al-Baqarah 2). From this verse, it is understood that free is killed for free, and slave for slave, and free includes both man and woman. (2) The hadith has passed that a Jew was crushed to death for a slave girl, from which it is understood that a man is killed for a woman. (Bukhari, chapter on stoning or beating to death). And that a free man is killed for a slave: evidence is the hadith of Samurah ibn Jundub that the Prophet (saw) said: 'Whoever kills his slave, we will kill him; and whoever mutilates his slave, we will mutilate him.' (Tirmidhi, Ibn Majah, Abu Dawood). From this hadith, it is understood that if a free man kills a slave, the free man is killed; and if a slave kills a free man, the slave is killed in qisas a fortiori. Imam Shafi'i says that a free man is not killed for a slave. Footnote: (a)... (b)... (c)... Their proof is the hadith of Ibn Abbas that the Prophet (saw) said: 'A free person is not killed for a slave.' (Darqutni, Bayhaqi). From this hadith, it is understood that a free man is not killed for a slave. And that a Muslim is killed for a kafir: evidence is the hadith of Ibn Umar that the Messenger of Allah (saw) killed a Muslim for a mu'ahid (treaty-protected person) and said: 'I am the most worthy to fulfill his covenant.' (Darqutni, Bayhaqi). From this, it is understood that a Muslim is killed for a kafir. Imam Shafi'i says that a Muslim is not killed for a kafir; rather, if a Muslim kills him, the diyah of the kafir is obligatory upon him. In a hadith: 'I asked Ali, do you have anything not in the Quran? ... He said: The bloodwit, the freeing of captives, and that a Muslim is not killed for a kafir.' (Bukhari, Abu Dawood). From this hadith, it is understood that a Muslim is not killed for a kafir. (2) Also, the blood of a kafir is permissible, so a Muslim is not killed for him; rather, his diyah is made obligatory.
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on qisas (retaliatory execution) in cases involving different categories of persons: free, slave, Muslim, and dhimmi (protected non-Muslim citizen). The author, commenting on the matn, first establishes that intentional murder necessitates qisas unless the guardian forgives. He then clarifies that three types of persons are not protected: the married adulterer, the murderer, and the apostate, citing the famous hadith. The core ruling is that a free person is killed for a free person (male or female), a free person for a slave, a slave for a free person, a slave for a slave, and a Muslim for a dhimmi. The proof is the Qur'anic verse on qisas (2:178) and several hadiths. A specific hadith about a Jew being killed for a slave girl demonstrates that a man can be killed for a woman. The hadith of Samurah establishes that a free person can be killed for killing a slave. The author then contrasts the Hanafi position with that of Imam Shafi'i, who holds that a free person is not killed for a slave, citing a hadith from Ibn Abbas. The Hanafi response here is implicit: the hadith of Samurah is taken as stronger or more specific. Similarly, for the case of Muslim killing a dhimmi, the Hanafi rely on the hadith of Ibn Umar where the Prophet killed a Muslim for a mu'ahid. The Shafi'i counter with the hadith of Ali that a Muslim is not killed for a kafir. The Hanafi conclude by stating that the kafir's blood is lawful (halal), so qisas is not applied; instead, only diyah (blood money) is due.

Key Terms
قصاص (qisas): Retaliatory punishment for intentional murder, where the killer is executed unless the guardian forgives.
ذمي (dhimmi): A non-Muslim living under the protection of the Islamic state, paying jizyah.
دية (diyah): Blood money paid to the victim's family as compensation when qisas is not applicable or is waived.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if a free Muslim man kills a dhimmi (protected non-Muslim)?
A) The free Muslim is executed in qisas.
B) He only pays diyah, no qisas.
C) He is not liable because the victim is a non-Muslim.
D) He must pay double diyah.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, qisas applies between different social and religious categories as specified by specific hadiths, except where a general hadith limits it.

Qisas — Retaliation
intermediate
6 min
No Qisas for Killing a Musta'man
Ruling with proof on qisas for musta'man

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a Muslim is not executed in qisas for killing a musta'man and identify when diyah is due.

Core Idea
A Muslim is not killed for a musta'man; only diyah applies because the musta'man's blood is not fully protected.

This passage addresses a specific category of homicide: a Muslim kills a non-Muslim who entered Islamic territory with temporary safe passage (aman). The Hanafi school rules that qisas (retaliatory execution) is not applicable; instead, only diyah (blood money) is required, and only if the victim's people have a treaty with Muslims. The ruling is supported by both the Qur'an and Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
Determine what action is being ruled upon (a Muslim killing a musta'man) and the hukm level: no qisas, only diyah.
The act is a killing, but the consequence is not execution; it is financial compensation.
2
Locate the Dalil
The author cites Qur'an 4:92 and the hadith 'A Muslim is not killed for a kafir'. Identify these sources.
The verse prescribes diyah and freeing a slave for a killing involving a treaty people.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
How does the verse prove no qisas? The verse mentions only diyah and freeing a slave, omitting qisas. This indicates qisas is not required.
The hadith is general: 'A Muslim is not killed for a kafir.' The musta'man is a kafir.
4
Note the Rationale
The musta'man comes from dar al-harb and the Islamic state has not undertaken responsibility for his protection; his blood is not fully protected.
This contrasts with a dhimmi, for whom a Muslim would be executed.
5
Evaluate the Thamarah al-Khilaf
If there is a treaty with the musta'man's people, diyah is due. If no treaty, the text implies no liability, though the killing is still haram.
The passage does not explicitly address the no-treaty case, but the reasoning suggests no diyah.

[2306] (13) And a Muslim is not killed for a musta'man. A Muslim is not killed for a person granted safe passage. A kafir from dar al-harb comes to dar al-Islam and a Muslim kills him; then for that musta'man, a Muslim is not killed. Rather, if there is a treaty with his people, his diyah is paid. Source pages p. 300

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on qisas when a Muslim kills a musta'man, i.e., a non-Muslim who enters the Islamic territory with temporary safe passage (aman). The author states that the Muslim is not executed in retaliation. Instead, only diyah (blood money) is due, and only if there is a treaty with the victim's people. The proof is the Qur'anic verse (4:92) which prescribes diyah and freeing of a slave for such cases, implying no qisas. Additionally, the general hadith 'A Muslim is not killed for a kafir' (previously cited) applies, as the musta'man is a kafir. The author argues that since the musta'man comes from dar al-harb and the Islamic state has not taken responsibility for his protection, his blood is not fully protected, thus qisas does not apply. This contrasts with a dhimmi, who is under permanent protection and for whom a Muslim would be executed.

Key Terms
مستأمن (musta'man): A non-Muslim from enemy territory (dar al-harb) who has been granted safe passage (aman) to enter Islamic territory temporarily.
دار الحرب (dar al-harb): Territory not under Islamic rule and not in a peace treaty with Muslims; enemy territory.

Key Takeaway
A musta'man's blood is not fully protected; a Muslim who kills him is not executed but must pay diyah only if the victim's people have a treaty with the Muslims.

Equality in Qisas: Man for Woman, Adult for Child
Hanafi ruling on equality in qisas supported by a hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on equality in qisas and explain the proof from the hadith of Anas.

Core Idea
In the Hanafi school, qisas is equal across gender, age, and ability — no life is worth less.

Qisas is a form of retributive justice, but does the victim's identity affect the punishment? This lesson examines the Hanafi position that a Muslim's life is equal regardless of gender, age, or physical condition. We will explore the ruling and its proof from the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Read the opening statement: a man is killed for a woman, an adult for a child, a healthy person for a blind/disabled person.
The ruling is broad — no distinction based on social or physical attributes.
2
Locate the Proof (Dalil)
The passage cites the hadith of Anas where the Prophet executed a Jewish man for killing a female slave.
This is a Sahih hadith from Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Analyze the Evidence (Wajh al-Dalalah)
The Prophet killed a man for a woman (and a slave). This shows that gender and status do not prevent qisas.
The principle: all protected lives (ma'sum al-dam) are equal in qisas.
4
Note the Scope
Equality covers gender, age (adult/child), and disability (blind/disabled).
The ruling applies to any intentional killing where the victim is a protected person.
5
Confirm the Authority
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school, based on Zahir al-Riwayah.
No intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; the ruling is relied upon for fatwa.

Commentary
This passage states the Hanafi ruling that qisas applies equally between all Muslims regardless of social or physical differences. A man is killed for killing a woman, an adult for a child, a healthy person for a blind or disabled person. The commentary explains that this is because they are equal in the deen (religion). The hadith of Anas is cited where the Prophet executed a Jewish man for killing a female slave (even though the victim was a woman and a slave). This proves that gender and physical condition are not barriers to qisas. The Hanafi school thus rejects any discrimination in qisas among Muslims.

Qisas — Retaliation
beginner
6 min
No Qisas for Father Killing Son or Master Killing Slave
Hanafi ruling with two prophetic hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a father is not subject to qisas for killing his son, nor a master for killing his slave, and explain the prophetic proofs that establish this exception.

Core Idea
A father is not executed for his son, nor a master for his slave; they must pay diyah and may receive tazir.

This lesson presents a well-established Hanafi ruling that removes qisas (retaliatory execution) in two specific relationships: father-son and master-slave. While the act of killing remains a crime, the punishment shifts from qisas to diyah (blood money) and tazir (discretionary punishment). The ruling is based on clear prophetic hadith and reflects the Islamic legal principles of respecting parental authority and property rights.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
Recognize that the text explicitly states: a man is not killed for his son, nor for his slave (including mudabbir, mukatab, and his son's slave). Instead, diyah becomes obligatory and tazir is imposed.
2
Examine the first hadith (parent-child)
The hadith from Ibn Abbas quotes the Prophet: 'A parent is not killed for a child.' This directly establishes the father-son qisas exception. Note that the word 'walad' encompasses sons and daughters.
3
Examine the second hadith (master-slave)
The hadith from 'Amr ibn Shu'ayb narrates that a man who intentionally killed his slave was flogged one hundred lashes, banished for a year, and ordered to free a slave. The Prophet did not apply qisas, proving the same exception for masters.
4
Apply to analogous categories
The text extends the ruling to mudabbir (slave promised freedom after master's death), mukatab (slave contracting for freedom), and the son's slave. All are considered property under the master's/father's authority, so no qisas.
5
Determine the consequences
Without qisas, the killer must pay diyah (blood money) to the victim's heirs. Additionally, the judge may impose tazir (e.g., flogging, imprisonment) as a discretionary punishment. The father's authority is preserved while ensuring justice.

[2308] (15) A man is not killed for his son, nor for his slave, nor for his mudabbir, nor for his mukatab, nor for his son's slave. If a father kills his son, then the father is not killed for the son; rather, diyah becomes obligatory. Or if a master kills his slave, the master is not killed for the slave; rather, diyah becomes obligatory and he will be punished with tazir. Because of the father's honor and respect, the father is not killed on account of the son. (2) There is a hadith: from Ibn Abbas from the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'Hudud are not established in the mosques, and a parent is not killed for a child.' (a) (Tirmidhi, Bab ma ja'a fi al-rajul yaqtulu ibnaha [?], p. 259, no. 1 140/; Ibn Majah, Bab la yuqtalu al-walid bi waladihi, no. (2666)). From this hadith it is understood that the father is not killed on account of the son. And for a slave, the master is not killed; its proof is this hadith: from 'Amr ibn Shu'ayb from his father from his grandfather that a man killed his slave intentionally, so the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, flogged him one hundred lashes, banished him for a year, and erased his share from the Muslims. In a narration of Darqutni: 'He did not execute him for him, and he commanded him to free a slave.' (b) (Darqutni, Kitab al-Hudud wa al-Diyat, vol. 3, p. 105, no. 3254; Ibn Majah, Bab hal yuqtalu al-hurr bi al-'abd, p. 1383, no. 2664). From this hadith it is understood that the master is not killed, rather diyah is taken from him. And a mudabbir and a mukatab are on the same level as a slave; so for killing them too, there is no qisas upon the master. And respect for the father over the child is necessary, so for killing the son's slave, the father is also not killed. (2) The hadith has passed: 'You and your property belong to your father; your children are from the best of your earnings.'

Footnote: (a) He said: Hudud are not established in mosques, and a parent is not killed for a child. (b) 'Amr ibn Shu'ayb said that a man killed his slave intentionally, so the Prophet flogged him one hundred lashes, banished him for a year, and removed his share from the Muslims. And in Darqutni's narration: he did not execute qisas on him and commanded him to free a slave.
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage covers the Hanafi ruling that a father is not subject to qisas for killing his son, nor a master for killing his slave. The commentary provides two hadith proofs: one from Ibn Abbas that a parent is not killed for a child, and another from 'Amr ibn Shu'ayb where the Prophet flogged a master for killing his slave but did not execute him. The ruling extends to mudabbir (slave promised freedom after master's death) and mukatab (slave contracted for freedom), as they are also property of the master. Additionally, a man is not killed for killing his son's slave, due to the father's authority. In all these cases, diyah (blood money) is obligatory along with tazir (discretionary punishment), but not qisas.

Key Terms
مدبر (mudabbir): A slave who has been promised freedom upon the master's death (tadbir contract).
مكاتب (mukatab): A slave under a kitabah contract, working to purchase his freedom.
تعزير (tazir): Discretionary punishment left to the judge's discretion for offenses without fixed hadd or qisas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a father is not executed in qisas for killing his son, nor a master for his slave; instead, diyah and tazir are obligatory.

Qisas — Retaliation
beginner

Equality in Qiṣāṣ: A Man Killed for a Woman, the Healthy for the Disabled
States the equality ruling in qiṣāṣ with hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on equality in qiṣāṣ between different categories of victims and cite the hadith proof.

Core Idea
All free Muslims are equal in qiṣāṣ: a man's life is taken for a woman's, and the healthy for the disabled.

The Hanafi school establishes that qiṣāṣ (retaliatory execution) applies equally between all free Muslims, regardless of gender, age, or physical condition. This principle is derived from the Prophet's ﷺ action in executing a Jewish man for killing a slave-girl. In this lesson, we will examine the ruling and its proof.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling: a man is killed for a woman, an adult for a child, and a healthy person for a blind or disabled person.
The ruling covers all categories of free Muslims.
2
Understand the underlying principle
Recognize that the basis is equality in religion (din). Physical differences like gender, age, or disability do not affect the sanctity of life.
This overrides considerations of blood money (diya) differences.
3
Examine the dalil
Locate the hadith from Anas ibn Malik where the Prophet ﷺ killed a Jew for murdering a slave-girl.
The hadith is from Sahih al-Bukhari and Sahih Muslim.
4
Extract the legal reasoning (wajh al-dalalah)
The Prophet's action demonstrates that the killer's gender or the victim's status does not prevent qiṣāṣ. This establishes equality in retaliation.
The dalil is specific but the principle is general.

A man is killed for a woman, and an adult for a child, and a healthy person for a blind and a disabled person. And a man will be killed for a woman, and an adult will be killed for a child, and a healthy person for a blind and a disabled person. These people are equal in terms of religion, so a man and a woman, and a small and a big, or a healthy and a disabled are not considered. Rather, each will be killed for the other. In a hadith, a Jewish man was crushed with a stone for killing a girl. From Anas ibn Malik that the Prophet ﷺ killed a Jew for a slave-girl he killed for her jewelry (Sahih al-Bukhari, chapter: Killing a man for a woman, p. 2017 no. 6885; Sahih Muslim, chapter: Establishing qiṣāṣ in killing with stones etc. p. 58 no. 1672).
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage states the Hanafi ruling on equality in qiṣāṣ (retaliatory killing) between different categories of victims. The ruling is that a man is killed for a woman, an adult for a child, and a healthy person for a blind or disabled person. The basis is that all these individuals are equal in the sight of Allah in terms of human life and sanctity (ḥurma). The text provides a hadith proof: the Prophet ﷺ executed a Jewish man for killing a slave-girl by crushing him with stones, establishing that the killer's gender or status does not prevent retaliation. The Hanafi school maintains that qiṣāṣ is established between all free Muslims regardless of physical condition or gender, as long as the killing is intentional and unjust.

Key Terms
جنايات (jināyāt): Crimes involving bodily harm or homicide; the book topic.
قصاص (qiṣāṣ): Retaliatory punishment, specifically execution for murder or amputation for intentional injury.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
All free Muslims are equal in qiṣāṣ, as established by the Prophet's ﷺ execution of a Jew for a slave-girl.

Qisas — Retaliation

Father Not Killed for Son, Master Not Killed for Slave
States exceptions where qiṣāṣ is not applied due to relationship or ownership

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a father is not executed for killing his son and apply the same principle to master-slave relationships, citing the textual proofs.

Core Idea
A father’s honor and a master’s ownership prevent qisas; only diya and ta‘zir apply.

This lesson examines two key exceptions to the general rule of qisas. The Hanafi school, relying on explicit hadith, holds that certain relationships—father-child and master-slave—create a legal impediment to qisas. Instead, the killer must pay blood money (diya) and receive discretionary punishment (ta‘zir).

Guided Path
1
Identify the exception cases
List the five cases where qisas is not applied: father kills son, master kills his slave, mudabbir, mukatab, or his son's slave.
The common thread is either direct lineal ascent or ownership.
2
Recognize the rationale
The father’s honor and the master’s right of ownership create a legal impediment (mani‘) to qisas.
This is based on the principle that a person is not subject to qisas for harming his own property in certain ways.
3
Examine the first hadith
The hadith from Ibn Abbas: 'لا يقتل الوالد بالولد' directly prohibits qisas of a father for his child.
This hadith is a clear prohibition (dalala qati‘) though its transmission (thubut) is zanni (ahad).
4
Examine the second hadith
The hadith of Amr ibn Shu‘ayb: a master intentionally killed his slave; the Prophet punished him with flogging, exile, and compensation but not qisas.
The absence of qisas in the Prophetic practice establishes the rule for slaves.
5
Apply the ruling
In any of these five cases, the penalty shifts from qisas to diya (mandatory) and ta‘zir (at the judge’s discretion).
The killer must also free a slave in the slave-killing case (according to one narration).

Source Text
