Qisas — Retaliation
intermediate
6 min
Qisas for Multiple Victims: One Hand Cut, One Hand Paid
States Hanafi ruling and refutes Shafi'i view on qisas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school cuts only one hand when an offender cuts the right hands of two victims, and refute the Shafi'i counter-argument using the same athar.

Core Idea
When qisas is impossible for all victims, the remaining claim is satisfied by diyah—not by cutting a different limb.

This lesson deals with a specific case in qisas: an offender cuts the right hands of two victims but has only one right hand. The Hanafi school rules that the victims collectively cut the offender's one right hand, and then share half the full diyah equally. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, arguing that both of the offender's hands should be cut. By examining the proofs, we will see how the Hanafi school defends its position using the same athar cited by the Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The offender cuts the right hands of two victims. The Hanafi ruling: the victims have the right to cut the offender's one right hand and then take half the diyah (blood money) from him, divided equally.
The diyah for a hand is half the full diyah (50 camels or equivalent).
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that both of the offender's hands must be cut—one for each victim.
The Shafi'i school relies on an athar from Ali (RA) about cutting hands of false witnesses.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i proof: an athar from Ali (RA) who said to two false witnesses, 'If I knew that both of you did it intentionally, I would cut both your hands.' They interpret this as a precedent for cutting both hands when two people are involved in a crime.
This athar is recorded in Sunan al-Bayhaqi and parts of Sahih al-Bukhari.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school responds that the athar is about false testimony (hadd for qadhf), not about qisas for bodily injury. Moreover, in an actual case of cutting hands, Ali (RA) imposed diyah for one hand, not qisas for both, as mentioned in the first athar.
The Hanafi response shows that the Shafi'i misinterpret the athar; it does not apply to this case.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under Hanafi law, only one hand is cut; under Shafi'i law, both hands would be cut.
This affects the extent of punishment and the amount of diyah.

Source Text

[۲۳۳۳] (۴۰) وان قطع واحد يمنى رجلين فحضرا فلهما ان يقطعا يده ويأخذا منه نصف الدية يقتسمانها نصفين (الف) (سن للمتقی باب الاثنین اوانچر يقطعان یدر جل معاج ثامن ،ص ۷۵، نمبر ۱۵۹۷۷ار بخاری شریف، باب اذا اصاب قوم من رجل هل يعاقب او يقتص منهم لهم ؟ ص ۰۱۸ انمبر ۶۸۹۶) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ حضرت علیؓ نے ایک ہاتھ کی دیت لازم کی۔ اس لئے دونوں پر آدھی آدھی دیت لازم ہوگی۔

ایک آدمی نے دو آدمیوں کے دائیں ہاتھ کاٹ ڈالے۔ اب کاٹنے والے کے پاس دو دائیں ہاتھ تو نہیں ہیں کہ ان کو جائے جائیں۔ اور یہاں دو آدمیوں کے دائیں ہاتھوں کا حق ہے۔ اس لئے دونوں کو یہ حق ہوگا کہ کاٹنے والے کا دایاں ہاتھ کاٹ لے جس سے دونوں مقطوع کے آدھے آدھے حق وصول ہو جائیں گے اور باقی آدھے آدھے حق کے لئے کاٹنے والے سے ایک ہاتھ کی دیت جو آدھی دیت یعنی پچاس اونٹ ہوتے ہیں وہ لے لے اور آپس میں آدھا آدھا یعنی پچیس پچیس اونٹ تقسیم کر لے۔ ایک آدمی کے دائیں ہاتھ کا بدلہ کاٹنے والے کا دایاں ہاتھ ہوا اور دوسرے آدمی کے دائیں ہاتھ کا بدلہ ایک آدمی کی آدھی دیت ہوئی۔ کیونکہ کاٹنے والے کے پاس دوسرا دایاں ہاتھ نہیں ہے جو کاٹا جا سکے۔ اور بایاں ہاتھ کاٹ نہیں سکتا۔ کیونکہ اس نے دونوں کے دائیں ہاتھ کاٹے ہیں۔ اس لئے یہی صورت باقی رہی کہ ہاتھ کی دیت لے جو پوری جان کی آدھی دیت ہوتی ہے۔ اور دونوں آدھی آدمی تقسیم کر لے
(۲) اوپر گزر چکا ہے کہ قصاص نہ لے سکے تو دیت لے گا۔
یمنی رجلین : دو آدمیوں کے دائیں ہاتھ دائیں ہاتھ ۔
Al-Sharh al-Thumayri, volume three, page 309, Book of Jinaayat. [2333] (40) And if one person cuts the right hands of two men and they both appear, then they have the right to cut his hand and take from him half the diyah, dividing it in half. (a) [Reference to Sunan al-Muttaqi etc.] From this athar it is understood that Ali, may Allah be pleased with him, made the diyah of one hand obligatory. Therefore, both are liable for half-half diyah. Imam al-Shafi'i says that both hands should be cut. He argues using the above athar. In it, he said: 'If I knew that both of you did it intentionally, I would cut both your hands.' From this it is understood that in qisas, both hands should be cut. [2333] (40) One man cut the right hands of two men. So when both come, they have the right to cut one of his hands and take from him half the diyah, dividing it half-half. One man cut the right hands of two men. Now the cutter does not have two right hands to be cut. And here two men have the right to his right hand. Therefore, both have the right to cut the cutter's right hand, so that both victims' half rights are received. And for the remaining half-rights, they take from the cutter the diyah of one hand, which is half the full diyah, i.e., fifty camels, and divide it half-half, i.e., twenty-five camels each. The right hand of one man is replaced by the cutter's right hand, and the right hand of the second man is replaced by half the diyah of a person. Because the cutter does not have another right hand to be cut, and he cannot cut the left hand because he cut both victims' right hands. So this remains: take the diyah of the hand, which is half the full diyah, and both divide it half-half. (2) It has already passed that if qisas cannot be taken, then diyah will be taken. Yumna rajulain: two men's right hands.
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hanafi school on a case of qisas (retaliatory amputation) when an offender cuts the right hands of two victims but has only one right hand. The Hanafi position is that the victims collectively have the right to cut the offender's one right hand, and then they share half of the full diyah (blood money) equally between them. The reason is that qisas can only be carried out on the exact limb cut, but since there are two victims and only one corresponding hand, qisas is performed once and the remaining claim is compensated with diyah. The passage then records a dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i, who argues that both of the offender's hands should be cut (one for each victim), citing an athar from Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) where he said, 'If I knew that both of you did it intentionally, I would cut both your hands.' The Hanafi response clarifies that the athar actually supports their position because Ali ordered the payment of diyah rather than cutting both hands. The Imam's conditional statement indicates that even if he had cut both hands, that would be a punishment for intentional false testimony, not a precedent for this case. Thus, the Hanafi ruling stands: when qisas is not fully possible, the remaining share is commuted to diyah.

Key Terms
يمنى رجلين (yumna rajulayn): The right hands of two men
نصف الدية (nisf al-diyya): Half of the full blood money (diyah) for a whole person
قصاص (qisas): Retaliatory punishment, e.g., cutting the hand for cutting a hand

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When one person cuts the right hands of two victims and he has only one right hand, what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) Both victims cut the offender's left hand as well
B) The victims cut the offender's right hand and share half the diyah equally
C) The offender pays full diyah to each victim
D) The offender's right hand is cut and the second victim receives full diyah

Key Takeaway
When qisas is impossible for all victims due to lack of corresponding limbs, the remaining claim is satisfied by diyah, not by retaliating with a different limb.

Qisas — Retaliation
intermediate
6 min
Ruling When Only One Victim Appears for Qisas
Ruling for one victim who cuts the offender's hand, leaving the other with diyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for the second victim when one victim has already taken qisas and identify the hadith that establishes the diyah amount for a hand.

Core Idea
If one victim carries out qisas, the other receives half diyah — the hand belongs to both collectively.

This lesson addresses a specific scenario in qisas: two victims have their hands cut by the same offender. One victim comes forward and cuts the offender's hand in retribution. When the second victim appears, the offender's hand is already severed. What is the second victim's right? The Hanafi school rules that he is entitled to half the full diyah (blood money), based on authoritative proofs. Understanding this ruling clarifies how qisas and diyah interact when the object of qisas is exhausted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the legal question
The scenario: an offender cuts the hands of two victims. One victim comes and cuts the offender's hand as qisas. The second victim arrives later. The question: what is the second victim's entitlement?
2
State the Hanafi ruling
The Hanafi ruling: the second victim receives half the full diyah from the offender. This is because the hand that was cut belonged to both victims collectively; when one took qisas, the other's share converted to diyah.
The ruling applies when qisas is no longer possible.
3
Examine the proof from hadith
The Prophet ﷺ decreed that for a hand, if cut, the diyah is half the full diyah (fifty camels or equivalent). This hadith directly establishes the amount for the second victim's claim.
The hadith is from Amr ibn Shu'aib: 'and for the hand if cut, half the diyah'.
4
Note the inter-madhhab disagreement
The Shafi'i school disagrees with this ruling. The passage defends the Hanafi view by citing the hadith and the athar of Ali (RA) to show that when qisas is impossible, diyah becomes obligatory.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi.

Commentary
This lesson deals with a further scenario: if only one of the two victims comes forward and carries out qisas on the offender's hand, then the other victim, who missed the opportunity, is entitled to half the diyah from the offender. The reasoning is that the hand that was cut belonged to both victims collectively (since the offender had injured both), so when one victim cuts it, the other's share is lost and must be compensated by diyah. The text provides an athar from Ibrahim that whenever qisas is not possible, diyah becomes obligatory. It also cites a hadith from the Prophet ﷺ specifying that the diyah for a hand is half the full diyah (fifty camels). This hadith establishes the amount of half diyah for the second victim.

Key Terms
نصف العقل (nisf al-'aql): Half the blood money (diyah)
عاقلته ('aaqilatuhu): His paternal male relatives (who are jointly liable for diyah)
قصاص (qisas): Retributive justice in kind for intentional injury or killing
دية (diyah): Blood money paid to the victim or heirs as compensation

Qisas — Retaliation
intermediate
8 min
Qisas upon confession of a slave for intentional murder
States that qisas is obligatory on a slave who confesses to murder

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a slave confesses to intentional murder, identify the Quranic verse and athar used as proof, and explain why the slave's confession is valid despite potential harm to the master.

Core Idea
A slave's confession to intentional murder makes qisas obligatory, even if it harms his master.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi position on a slave who confesses to intentional murder. While some might question the validity of such a confession due to the master's property rights, the school holds that the slave's life is at stake and the confession is taken at face value. We will see the Quranic and athar proofs that establish this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is a slave confessing to intentional murder (qatl al-amd). The ruling is that qisas (retaliatory killing) becomes obligatory upon the slave.
The confession (iqrar) is the trigger; qisas is the prescribed punishment.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The primary dalil is the Quranic verse (Surah al-Baqarah 2:178) which prescribes qisas for a slave killed by a slave. Additional athar from Ali and Ibrahim directly state that qisas applies to a slave for intentional murder.
The Quranic text is qat'i al-thubut and qat'i al-dalala (definitive in transmission and meaning).
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'al-ʿabdu bi-l-ʿabdi' (the slave for the slave) in the verse makes clear that qisas is applicable when a slave is killed by a slave. The athar confirm that even if the victim is a free person, qisas is due on the slave killer.
The verse implies equality in retaliation regardless of social status.
4
Address the potential doubt
A doubt arises: the slave might confess falsely to spite his master by causing loss. The Hanafi response is that this doubt is not considered because the slave's life is at stake; the confession is his own act and is credible.
The master's financial loss is secondary to the principle of justice and the validity of the confession.

Commentary
This lesson deals with the ruling on a slave who confesses to intentional murder. The Hanafi position is that qisas becomes obligatory upon him, even though it may cause financial loss to his master. The proof is from the Quranic verse that prescribes qisas for a slave (implying a slave can be killed in retaliation for a slave) and from athar of Ali and Ibrahim which state that qisas applies to a slave. The passage notes a potential doubt: the slave might be confessing falsely to harm his master. However, this doubt is rejected because the life of the slave is at stake, and the confession is taken at face value. The slave's soul is his own, and the master's loss is secondary.

Key Terms
اقرار (iqrar): Confession of a crime, which triggers liability.
قود (qawd): Qisas (retaliatory killing) - synonym of qisas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) The confession is invalid because it harms the master.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling that a slave's confession to intentional murder obligates qisas, based on direct scriptural evidence and the principle that the slave's life outweighs the master's property.

Qisas — Retaliation
beginner
6 min
Qisas and diyah when a single arrow kills two men
Ruling for one arrow that kills intended and unintended victims

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a single intentional act causing multiple deaths and explain why qisas applies to the intended victim and diyah to the unintended.

Core Idea
Intent to each victim determines the liability: qisas for intended, diyah for unintended.

This lesson addresses a scenario where a person intentionally shoots an arrow that penetrates one man and then kills another. The Hanafi school distinguishes between the intended victim and the unintended one, assigning qisas for the first and diyah for the second. Understanding this distinction is crucial in crimes involving multiple victims.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the victims
The act is a single intentional shooting. There are two victims: the first (the intended target) and the second (the unintended victim).
The arrow passes through the first and hits the second.
2
Determine intent for each victim
The archer intended to kill the first victim. The killing of the second was unintentional, though the act itself was intentional.
Intent is toward a specific person, not toward all possible consequences.
3
Apply the ruling
For the intended killing, qisas (retaliation) is obligatory. For the unintended killing, diyah (blood money) is due.
4
Identify the governing principle
The principle is that qisas requires specific intent; when killing is unintentional, diyah substitutes.
This is supported by general proofs from Quran and Sunnah about intentional and accidental killing.
5
Note the evidentiary basis
The text cites hadith and athar establishing diyah for unintended harm, such as the hadith on diyah for organs, and the principle that when qisas is impossible, diyah is obligatory.
The proofs are general and applied to this specific case by analogy.

[ ۲۳۳۶] (۴۳) و من رمى رجلا عمدا فنفذ السهم منه الى آخر فماتا فعليه القصاص للاول والدية كاٹنے کے لئے دایاں ہاتھ باقی نہیں رہا۔ اس لئے اب وہ اپنے ہاتھ کے لئے دیت لے گا۔ پہلے گزر چکا ہے کہ قصاص کے لئے کچھ نہ ہو تو دیت لے گا۔ عن ابراهيم قال ما كان من جرح من العمد لا يستطاع فيه القصاص فهو على الجارح في ماله دون عاقلته ( الف ) ( مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ۱۰۱ العمد الذي لا يستطاع فيه القصاص ج خامس میں ۲۰۳ نمبر ۲۷۴۰۴) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ جہاں قصاص لینا ممکن نہیں وہاں دیت لازم ہے۔ اور ایک ہاتھ کے لئے پوری جان کی آدھی دیت ہے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن عمر بن شعيب عن ابيه عن جده ... وقضى رسول الله لل الله في الانف اذا جدع الدية كاملة وان جدعت ثندؤته فنصف العقل خمسون من الابل او عدلها من الذهب او الورق او مائة بقرة او الف شلة وفي اليد اذا قطعت نصف العقل وفي الرجل نصف العقل (ب) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب دیات الاعضاء ص ۲۷۸ نمبر ۴۵۶۴ رنسائی شریف ، ذکر حدیث عمرو بن حزم في العقول و اختلاف الناقلین لرص ۶۶۸ نمبر ۴۸۵۸) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ایک ہاتھ کے لئے آدھی دیت یعنی پچاس اونٹ ہے۔
(۲۳۳۶] (۴۳) کسی نے جان بوجھ کر تیر مارا۔ پس تیر پار ہو کر دوسرے آدمی کو بھی لگا تو اس پر پہلے کے لئے قصاص ہے اور دوسرے کے لئے
حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت ابراہیم نے فرمایا جان بوجھ کر ایسا زخم لگایا جس کا قصاص نہیں لیا جا سکتا ہو تو زخم کرنے والے پر اس کے مال میں ہے نہ کہ خاندان پر (ب) حضور نے ناک کے بارے میں یہ فیصلہ فرمایا کہ جب کائی جائے تو پوری دیت ہے اور اس کا پستان کا نا تو آدھی دیت ہے پچاس اونٹ یا اس کے برابر سونا یا چاندی یا ایک سو گائے یا ایک ہزار بری اور ہاتھ کاٹا جائے تو آدھی دیت ہے اور پاؤں میں آدھی دیت ہے (ج) اے ایمان والو تم پر قصاص فرض کیا گیا ہے قتل میں آزاد آزاد کے بدلے ، غلام غلام کے بدلے اور مؤنث مؤنث کے بدلے (د) حضرت علیؓ نے فرمایا اگر غلام آزاد کو قتل کرے اور مقتول کے اولیاء کے پاس معاملہ جائے پس چاہے تو قتل کرے اور چاہے تو چھوڑ دے (ہ) حضرت ابراہیم نے فرمایا غلام جان بوجھ کر قتل کرے تو اس میں قصاص ہے۔
[2336] (43) And if a person intentionally shoots an arrow and it passes through one man to another and both die, then upon him is qisas for the first and diyah for the second. [The proof from previous lesson continues: hadith and athar about diyah for a hand]. (2336] (43) Someone intentionally shot an arrow. It passed through and hit another person. So for the first, qisas is due, and for the second, diyah. Footnotes: (a) Ibrahim said: Any intentional wound for which qisas is not possible is upon the injurer in his wealth, not on his aqila. (b) The Prophet decreed concerning the nose... (c) Qisas is prescribed for you... (d) Ali said: If a slave kills a free man... (e) Ibrahim said: A slave who commits intentional murder, there is qisas in it.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This lesson addresses a scenario where a person intentionally fires an arrow that penetrates one person and then hits another, killing both. The Hanafi ruling is that the archer is subject to qisas (retaliation) for the first victim because he intended to kill him (the arrow was aimed at him), but for the second victim, since the killing was unintentional (the arrow passed through accidentally), he must pay diyah (blood money). The text does not provide an explicit proof for this specific case within the passage, but it relies on the general principle that intentional acts attract qisas, while unintended consequences attract diyah. The footnotes reaffirm principles: when qisas is not possible, diyah is obligatory; and the hadith specifies the diyah for a hand, which is half the full diyah, though this hadith was originally cited for the previous lesson. The footnotes also include relevant Quranic verses and athar about qisas for slaves, which are general proofs.

Key Terms
فنفذ السهم (fa-nafadha al-sahm): The arrow penetrated (the first victim) and went through to another
قصاص (qisas): Retaliatory punishment, same meaning as in previous lessons.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person intentionally shoots an arrow that kills the intended target and also kills an unintended person, what are the consequences?
A) Qisas for both
B) Diyah for both
C) Qisas for the first and diyah for the second
D) No liability for the second

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a single intentional act that kills both the intended and unintended victims results in qisas for the intended and diyah for the unintended.

Qisas — Retaliation
intermediate
7 min
Slave's Confession to Willful Murder Requires Qisas
Ruling with proof for qisas on a slave's confession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a slave's confession to willful murder, identify the Quranic and athar proofs that establish qisas, and explain why the potential harm to the master is disregarded.

Core Idea
A slave's confession to willful murder is fully valid and leads to qisas, even if it harms the master.

This passage from Al-Sharh al-Sameri addresses a specific question: what happens when a slave confesses to intentional murder? The Hanafi school holds that the confession is accepted and qisas becomes obligatory. The text provides Quranic and athar proofs, and dismisses the objection that the slave might be acting against the master's interest. Let's examine the legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and the act
The ruling is that qisas is necessary (lazima) when a slave confesses to 'amd (intentional) murder.
The act is 'iqrar' (confession) to 'qatl al-'amd'.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The Quranic verse (2:178) is cited: 'wal-'abdu bil-'abdi' — slave for slave.
This establishes the principle of equality in qisas, including slaves.
3
Examine the supporting athar
Two athar: from 'Ali (heirs can choose qisas or pardon) and from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i (qisas for a slave's intentional killing).
These reinforce that a slave's life is subject to qisas.
4
Analyze the response to the doubt
The text addresses the doubt that the slave might be harming his master by giving his life, but dismisses it because the slave's life is at stake.
The master's property interest is outweighed by the gravity of the crime and confession.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[ ۲۳۳۵] (۴۲) واذا اقر العبد بقتل العمد لزمه القود اگر غلام قتل عمد کا اقرار کرے تو اس پر قصاص لازم ہے۔ اثر میں ہے کہ غلام اقرار کر لے کہ میں نے قتل عمد کیا ہے تو اس پر قصاص لازم ہوگا چاہے اس سے آقا کا نقصان ہو۔ آیت میں ہے۔ يا ايها الذين امنوا كتب عليكم القصاص في القتلى الحر بالحر والعبد بالعبد والانثى بالانثى (ج) (آیت ۷۸ سورۃ البقرۃ ۲) اس آیت میں ہے کہ غلام غلام کے بدلے قصاصا قتل کیا جائے گا (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ عن على قال اذا قتل العبد الحر رفع الى اولياء المقتول فان شاؤا قتلوا وان شاؤا استحيوا (ر) (سنن المتفق، باب العبد يقتل الحر خامس ہیں ۲۸ نمبر ۱۵۹۶۱) عن ابراهيم فى العبد عمدا قال فيه القود (ه) ( كتاب الآثار، باب جراحات العبد ص ۱۲۶ نمبر ۵۸۲) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ غلام قتل عمد کا اقرار کرے تو اس پر قصاص لازم ہے۔ اس میں یہ شبہ بھی ہے کہ غلام قتل عمد کا اقرار کر کے اپنی جان دینا چاہتا ہے اور آقا کا نقصان کرنا چاہتا ہے لیکن چونکہ غلام کی جان جا رہی ہے اس لئے اس شبہ کی طرف توجہ نہیں کی جائے گی۔
[2335] (42) And if a slave confesses to willful murder, qisas is necessary for him. If a slave confesses to willful murder, then qisas is necessary for him, even if it causes harm to the master. The verse: 'O you who believe, qisas is prescribed for you in cases of murder: the free for the free, the slave for the slave, and the female for the female.' In this verse, it is that a slave is killed in exchange for a slave. (2) An athar: From 'Ali: He said, 'If a slave kills a free person, the case is referred to the heirs of the slain: if they wish, they kill him; if they wish, they spare him.' From Ibrahim regarding a slave [who kills] intentionally, he said: 'In it is qisas.' From these athar it became known that if a slave confesses to willful murder, qisas is necessary for him. Here there is also a doubt that the slave intends to give his life and cause loss to the master, but since the slave's life is being taken, this doubt is not considered.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof for the case of a slave confessing to willful murder. The matn states: if a slave confesses to 'amd (intentional) murder, qisas is necessary for him. The commentary explains that the slave's confession is accepted regardless of harm to the master. Proofs are given: first, the Quranic verse (2:178) which establishes qisas equality between free and slave. Second, an athar from 'Ali that the heirs of the deceased have the option to execute the slave or pardon him. Third, an athar from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i that intentional killing by a slave entails qisas. The text also addresses a potential objection: that the slave might be trying to harm his master by giving his own life; but since the life of the slave is at stake, this doubt is dismissed. Thus, the Hanafi position is that a slave's confession to willful murder is fully valid and leads to qisas.

Key Terms
عبد ('abd): A male slave; in this context, a slave who commits murder
اقرار (iqrar): Confession, admission of guilt by the accused
القود (al-qawad): Qisas, retaliation in kind for murder or bodily harm

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the potential harm to the master not considered when a slave confesses to willful murder?
A) Because the master's consent is required
B) Because the slave's life is at stake
C) Because the confession must be verified
D) Because the master can prevent the confession

Key Takeaway
A slave's confession to willful murder is fully valid and necessitates qisas, with any doubt about harm to the master dismissed as less weighty than the life at stake.
